mindmapping	<p>Tony Buzan, the author of many books, popularized the term <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mind_map" rel="nofollow noreferrer">mind map</a> for use in creating diagrams for visual representation of information. It is very commonly used technique for brain storming. Starting with a topic at the center, the diagram is developed by connecting it to related information. There are many <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_concept-_and_mind-mapping_software" rel="nofollow noreferrer">software tools available for mind mapping</a>, including many free ones. Many of these allow users to write scripts to access the mind maps and enhance the tool.</p>&#xA;

suppression	<p>Suppression is a form of technical filtering (e.g. of alert messages, signals, ...) where some output is withheld from being displayed after being generated in order to reduce the overall amount of information. Compared to filtering, the suppressed items are not thrown away, they get just not displayed. This could be due to user's configuration/customization in some system settings or profile, configured by a set of rules.</p>&#xA;
invisible	<blockquote class="spoiler">&#xA;  <p>    The <code>invisible</code> tag is intended to bring attention and association to all things not meeting the basic criteria of being self-evident to the naked eye. This would include anything hidden from view by another physical object, displaced to an area that is not observable by regular means or something that simply does not reflect the visible spectrum of light through transparency or gravitational lensing.&#xA;<br>&#xA;<br>&#xA;    This tag does not imply the motivation behind nor the root cause of the invisibility and none should be inferred.</p>&#xA;</blockquote>&#xA;
medium-trust	<p>Trust level refers to permissions set in the Web.config file that dictate what operations can and cannot be performed by Web applications. ASP.NET 3.5 and 4.0 shared hosting servers use the default Medium trust level with the addition of OleDbPermission, OdbcPermission, and a less-restrictive WebPermission.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Applications operating under a Medium trust level have no registry access, no access to the Windows event log, and cannot use ReflectionPermission (but can use Reflection). Such applications can communicate only with a defined range of network addresses and file system access is limited to the application's virtual directory hierarchy.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Using a Medium trust level prevents applications from accessing shared system resources and eliminates the potential for application interference. Adding OleDbPermission and OdbcPermission allows applications to use those data providers to access databases. WebPermission is modified to allow outbound http and https traffic.</p>&#xA;

The keys may be identical or there may be a&#xA;  simple transformation to go between the two keys.</p>&#xA;</blockquote>&#xA;&#xA;<p>as stated in <a href="https://www.google.com/url?sa=t&amp;rct=j&amp;q=&amp;esrc=s&amp;source=web&amp;cd=2&amp;cad=rja&amp;uact=8&amp;ved=0ahUKEwju4eagsorPAhWypYMKHb5BBGEQFggjMAE&amp;url=https%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FSymmetric-key_algorithm&amp;usg=AFQjCNGayTr8wwKxYxgY77ZWxweFIkh5FA&amp;sig2=lfZiEKlyCd9Oofsgi5ADCQ" rel="nofollow">Wikipedia</a>.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Since this tag is used in its general meaning, it would be a good idea to use one or more tags too, to describe your specific case better.</p>&#xA;

click-through	<h2>Description</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Click-through means that you can click <em>through</em> something. &#xA;Normally, the things behind it can then be clicked (or selected), while normally they wouldn't be clickable, because the element in front of it would catch the click-event <strong>[1]</strong>.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<hr>&#xA;&#xA;<h2>CSS</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<p>To make something click-through in CSS, many use <code>pointer-events: none;</code>, which means that, when an element is clicked,  a pointer event <em>(in this case, a click-event <strong>[1]</strong>)</em>  will not be fired. &#xA;Instead, you can click (or select) the elements behind it. This is basically useful for (partly or semi-)transparent images.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>It is also used to simply disable click-functionality (disabled links for example). <strong>Mind though</strong>, when using <code>pointer-events: none;</code> you disable all pointer events, not only the click-event (which is necessary for a click-through element); hovers and other pointer events will be ignored as well.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><strong>[1]</strong> Basically an event saying "Hey, I have been clicked!".</p>&#xA;

google-widget	<p>Definition from <a href="http://whatis.techtarget.com/definition/widget" rel="nofollow">Tech Target</a></p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>In computers, a widget is an element of a graphical user interface ( gui ) that displays information or provides a specific way for a user to interact with the operating system and application . Widgets include icons, pull-down menus, buttons, selection boxes, progress indicators, on-off checkmarks, scroll bars, windows, window edges (that let you resize the window), toggle buttons, forms, and many other devices for displaying information and for inviting, accepting, and responding to user actions.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>In programming, a widget also means the small program that is written in order to describe what a particular widget looks like, how it behaves, and how it interacts in response to user actions. Most operating systems include a set of ready-to-tailor widgets that a programmer can incorporate in an application, specifying how it is to behave. New widgets can be created. The term was apparently applied first in UNIX -based operating systems and the X Window System . In object-oriented programming ( oop ), each type of widget is defined as a class (or a subclass under a broad generic widget class) and is always associated with a particular window. In the AIX Enhanced X-Window Toolkit, a widget is the fundamental data type .</p>&#xA;

dbtable	<p><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Table_(database)" rel="nofollow">Database tables</a> store data in rows and columns.  The columns are defined when the table is created while rows are inserted, updated, and deleted by users over time.  These tables are often designed with some particularly kind of efficiency or checking in mind, depending on the data and how it will be added.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>For example, one could build the table with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database_index" rel="nofollow">indexes</a> to support efficient searching for specific values or with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database_trigger" rel="nofollow">triggers</a> to perform additional actions or validation when certain events occur, such as inserting a row into the table.</p>&#xA;

graphical-language	<p>There is a conflation of the terms <em>visual programming language (VPL)</em> and <em>graphical programming language</em>, and although there is a <a href="http://c2.com/cgi/wiki?GraphicalProgrammingLanguage" rel="nofollow">distinction between the two</a>, more work is needed to clarify the distinction between the two terms. The consensus seems to be that in graphical languages, the visual components <em>are</em> code elements, while <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visual_programming_language" rel="nofollow">visual programming</a> enables traditional languages to be manipulated <em>via</em> a graphical interface. onkeypress	<p>Unlike other key events in javascript, <code>keypress</code> may capture the actual character, that would be inserted in text field (only applies on editable elements, like text fields and content-editable html elements). This is hidint under <code>event.charCode</code>. On other events, such as <code>keyup</code> and <code>keydown</code> you only may capture ID of the key - with different systems, and languages, the same number may mean totally different characters.<br>&#xA;On the other side, <code>keypress</code> along with <code>keyup</code> may not block many default event actions - like pressing <kbd>tab</kbd>, <kbd>F5</kbd> or arrows.</p>&#xA;

nameservers	<p>In computing, a name server (also spelled nameserver) is a program or computer server that implements a name-service protocol. It maps a human-recognizable identifier to a system-internal, often numeric, identification or addressing component.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The Internet maintains two principal namespaces, the domain name hierarchy<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nameserver" rel="nofollow">1</a> and the Internet Protocol (IP) address system.[2] The Domain Name System maintains the domain namespace and provides translation services between these two namespaces. Internet name servers implement the Domain Name System.[3] A DNS name server is a server that stores the DNS records, such as address (A, AAAA) records, name server (NS) records, and mail exchanger (MX) records for a domain name (see also List of DNS record types) and responds with answers to queries against its database.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The top hierarchy of the Internet Domain Name System is served by the root name servers maintained by delegation by the Internet Corporation for Assigned Names and Numbers (ICANN).</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nameserver" rel="nofollow">source</a></p>&#xA;
microsoft-commerce-server	<p>Microsoft Commerce Server is a Microsoft product for building e-commerce systems. It uses Microsoft .NET technology.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The latest release of the product is Commerce Server 2009. It was launched at the National Retail Federation (NRF) in New York in January 2009, with its official launch at the MIX09 event in Las Vegas in March 2009.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>With its inaugural release in 2000, Commerce Server replaced Microsoft Site Server, expanding on the functionality of it and establishing a focus on e-commerce functionality (rather than concerning itself with document management or content metadata). It helps create e-commerce solutions and Web sites with high-performance, familiar tools that simplify setup, management, and administration tasks.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Commerce Server 2009, which became available on Microsoft's price list on April 1, 2009, introduced multi-channel awareness into the product, a new default site (running in Microsoft's SharePoint product) - including 30 new web parts and controls, and WYSIWYG (what-you-see-is-what-you-get) editing experiences for business people and site designers.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>These features were introduced through the new Commerce Foundation - a new abstraction layer which unifies calling patterns of the core systems (see below) and allows for different presentation and business logic to be easily added and represented as 'selling channels'; and SharePoint Commerce Services which includes integration with Microsoft SharePoint - a new default site with 30 new web parts and controls pre-assembled. The default site can be skinned through the new page templating technology, allowing for individual pages to be easily changed by selecting a different template.</p>&#xA;
lead	<p>Accesses data from a subsequent row in the same result set without the use of a self-join in SQL Server 2017. LEAD provides access to a row at a given physical offset that follows the current row. Use this analytic function in a SELECT statement to compare values in the current row with values in a following row. </p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>For further reading &#xA;<a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/sql/t-sql/functions/lead-transact-sql" rel="nofollow noreferrer">https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/sql/t-sql/functions/lead-transact-sql</a></p>&#xA;
sar	<p><strong>Usage:</strong></p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>sar [ -A ] [ -b ] [ -B ] [ -C ] [ -d ] [ -h ] [ -i interval ] [ -m ] [ -p ] [ -q ] [ -r ] [ -R ] [ -S ] [ -t ] [ -u [ ALL ] ] [ -v ] [ -V ] [ -w ] [ -W ] [ -y ] [ -n { keyword [,...] | ALL } ] [ -I { int [,...] | SUM | ALL | XALL } ] [ -P { cpu [,...] | ALL } ] [ -o [ filename ] | -f [ filename ] ] [ -s [ hh:mm:ss ] ] [ -e [ hh:mm:ss ] ] [ interval [ count ] ]&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p><strong>Description:</strong></p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The <code>sar</code> command writes to standard output the contents of selected cumulative activity counters in the operating system. The accounting system, based on the values in the <code>count</code> and <code>interval</code> parameters, writes information the specified number of times spaced at the specified intervals in seconds. If the <code>interval</code> parameter is set to zero, the <code>sar</code> command displays the average statistics for the time since the system was started. If the <code>interval</code> parameter is specified without the <code>count</code> parameter, then reports are generated continuously. The collected data can also be saved in the file specified by the <code>-o filename</code> flag, in addition to being displayed onto the screen. If <code>filename</code> is omitted, <code>sar</code> uses the standard system activity daily data file, the <code>/var/log/sa/sadd</code> file, where the <code>dd</code> parameter indicates the current day. By default all the data available from the kernel are saved in the data file.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The <code>sar</code> command extracts and writes to standard output records previously saved in a file. This file can be either the one specified by the <code>-f</code> flag or, by default, the standard system activity daily data file.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Without the <code>-P</code> flag, the <code>sar</code> command reports system-wide (global among all processors) statistics, which are calculated as averages for values expressed as percentages, and as sums otherwise. If the <code>-P</code> flag is given, the <code>sar</code> command reports activity which relates to the specified processor or processors. If <code>-P ALL</code> is given, the <code>sar</code> command reports statistics for each individual processor and global statistics among all processors.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>You can select information about specific system activities using flags. Not specifying any flags selects only CPU activity. Specifying the <code>-A</code> flag is equivalent to specifying <code>-bBdqrRSvwWy -I SUM -I XALL -n ALL -u ALL -P ALL</code>.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The default version of the <code>sar</code> command (CPU utilization report) might be one of the first facilities the user runs to begin system activity investigation, because it monitors major system resources. If CPU utilization is near 100 percent (user + nice + system), the workload sampled is CPU-bound.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>If multiple samples and multiple reports are desired, it is convenient to specify an output file for the <code>sar</code> command. Run the <code>sar</code> command as a background process. The syntax for this is:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>sar -o datafile interval count &gt;/dev/null 2&gt;&amp;1 &amp;&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>All data is captured in binary form and saved to a file (<code>datafile</code>). The data can then be selectively displayed with the <code>sar</code> command using the <code>-f</code> option. Set the <code>interval</code> and <code>count</code> parameters to select <code>count</code> records at <code>interval</code> second intervals. If the <code>count</code> parameter is not set, all the records saved in the file will be selected. Collection of data in this manner is useful to characterize system usage over a period of time and determine peak usage hours.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Note: The <code>sar</code> command only reports on local activities.</p>&#xA;

nbehave	<p>Based on Dan North's initial vision of rbehave and utilizing the behavioral domain specific language (DSL) of Behavior Driven Design (BDD) <a href="http://nbehave.codeplex.com/" rel="nofollow" title="The NBehave Team">we</a> created the NBehave framework.<br>&#xA;The primary goal of NBehave is a framework for defining and executing application requirement goals. These characterizations are modeled after the Behavioral Driven Design (BDD) terms Story, Scenario, Given, When, Then.<br>&#xA;Relying on a syntax that is lightweight and targeted at product owners (a few "quotes" mostly), the code becomes an executable and self-describing requirements document.<br>&#xA;The definitions within the actual unit test of the application coupled with the organic nature of the architecture and ubiquity of the domain model translates these concepts into becoming one cohesive amalgam.<br>&#xA;With the help of Domain Driven Design, the code actually becomes what we have always wanted, living requirements that are constantly asserted on to ensure their viability and accuracy from inception to implementation.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<h2>Example Code</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<blockquote>&#xA;  <p>NBehave V0.5, C#, NUnit V2.4.3</p>&#xA;</blockquote>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>using NBehave.Narrator.Framework;&#xA;using NBehave.Spec.NUnit;&#xA;&#xA;[ActionSteps]&#xA;public class UserLogsInSuccessfully&#xA;{&#xA;    // some code to setup _currentPage&#xA;    // ...&#xA;&#xA;    [Given("I am not logged in")]&#xA;    public void LogOut()&#xA;    {&#xA;        _currentPage.click("logout");&#xA;    }&#xA;&#xA;    [When("I log in as $username with a password $password")]&#xA;    public void LogIn(string username, string password)&#xA;    {&#xA;        _currentPage.click("login");&#xA;    }&#xA;&#xA;    [Then("I should see a message, \"$message\"")]&#xA;    public void CheckMessage(string message)&#xA;    {&#xA;        _currentPage.ToString().ShouldContain(message);&#xA;    }&#xA;}&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Along with a scenario:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>Given I am not logged in&#xA;When I log in as Morgan with a password SecretPassw0rd&#xA;Then I should see a message, "Welcome, Morgan!" &#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>And running the sceanrio as:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>&gt;NBehave-Console.exe  NameOfDll.dll /sf=user_logs_in_successfully.feature&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Produces the following output:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>NBehave version 0.4.5.183&#xA;Copyright Â© NBehave 2007-2009&#xA;All Rights Reserved.&#xA;&#xA;Runtime Environment -&#xA;   OS Version: Microsoft Windows NT 5.1.2600 Service Pack 3&#xA;  CLR Version: 2.0.50727.3603&#xA;&#xA;Scenario: 1.user_logs_in_successfully&#xA;Given I am not logged in - PENDING&#xA;When I log in as Morgan with a password SecretPassw0rd - PENDING&#xA;Then I should see a message, "Welcome, Morgan!" - PENDING&#xA;&#xA;P&#xA;Scenarios run: 1, Failures: 0, Pending: 1&#xA;Steps 3, failed 0, pending 3&#xA;&#xA;Pending:&#xA;1)  (1.user_logs_in_successfully): No matching Action found for "Given I am not logged in"&#xA;No matching Action found for "When I log in as Morgan with a password SecretPassw0rd"&#xA;No matching Action found for "Then I should see a message, "Welcome, Morgan!""&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p><em>This has been reproduced without the express permission of the NBehave Team, but it is such a useful test tool, I hope they don't mind :)</em>  </p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Check out <a href="http://nbehave.codeplex.com/wikipage?title=Getting%20started" rel="nofollow">http://nbehave.codeplex.com/wikipage?title=Getting%20started</a> to get started.</p>&#xA;

negotiate	<p>The <em>Negotiate</em> HTTP authentication scheme is defined in <a href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc4559" rel="nofollow">RFC 4559</a>.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>If a server receives a request for a protected resource it responds with status <code>401 Unauthorized</code> and a <code>WWW-Authenticate: Negotiate</code> header.  The client reissues the original request with a <code>WWW-Authenticate: Negotiate [gssapi-data]</code> header.  The server uses the <code>gssapi-data</code> to attempt to authenticate the client; if successful the request continues and a <code>2xx</code> response can also carry a <code>WWW-Authenticate</code> response header containing the final leg of an authentication.</p>&#xA;

par	<p>par is a paragraph reformatter, vaguely similar to fmt, but better. It can format, justify, align, slice and dice using a bewildering array of options. See <a href="http://www.nicemice.net/par/" rel="nofollow">http://www.nicemice.net/par/</a></p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>par is a filter which copies its input to its output, changing all white characters (except newlines) to spaces, and reformatting each paragraph.  Paragraphs are separated by protected, blank, and bodiless lines (see the Terminology section for definitions), and optionally delimited by indentation (see the d option in the Options section). Each output paragraph is generated from the corresponding input paragraph as follows:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ol>&#xA;<li>An optional prefix and/or suffix is removed from each input line.</li>&#xA;<li>The remainder is divided into words (separated by spaces).</li>&#xA;<li>The words are joined into lines to make an eye-pleasing paragraph.</li>&#xA;<li>The prefixes and suffixes are reattached.</li>&#xA;</ol>&#xA;&#xA;<p>If there are suffixes, spaces are inserted before them so that they all end in the same column.</p>&#xA;

direct3d10	<p>Originally called WGF 2.0 (Windows Graphics Foundation 2.0), then DirectX 10 and DirectX Next, Direct3D 10 features an updated shader model 4.0 and optional interruptibility for shader programs. In this model shaders still consist of fixed stages as on previous versions, but all stages support a nearly unified interface, as well as a unified access paradigm for resources such as textures and shader constants. The language itself has been extended to be more expressive, including integer operations, a greatly increased instruction count, and more C-like language constructs. In addition to the previously available vertex and pixel shader stages, the API includes a geometry shader stage that breaks the old model of one vertex in/one vertex out, to allow geometry to actually be generated from within a shader, allowing for complex geometry to be generated entirely on the graphics hardware.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Windows XP does not support DirectX 10 and above.</p>&#xA;

writeablebitmap	<p>Bitmaps are generally implemented as immutable objects in WPF. What this means is that once you create a  bitmap you can't make any changes to it. You can manipulate bitmaps by creating new versions, which then immediately become immutable and sometimes this is a good way to work.&#xA;Immutable bitmaps can be very efficient unless you want to indulge in a lot of dynamic changes in which case the overhead of creating and destroying them rapidly becomes too expensive. In this situation you need something a little more flexible - the WriteableBitmap.&#xA;The WriteableBitmap, as its name suggests, isn't immutable and you can get at its individual pixels and manipulate them as much as you want. This is the ideal way to work when you need dynamic bitmaps. So lets take a look at WriteableBitmap, how it works and how to use it to do dynamic things.&#xA;Notice that the WriteableBitmap class in Silverlight is very different to the same class in WPF.&#xA;To use WriteableBitmap we need to add:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>using System.Windows.Media.Imaging;&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>which contains all of the additional bitmap facilities we need.&#xA;You can create a WriteableBitmap in two ways. The most commonly used is to simply specify the size and format of the bitmap:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code> WriteableBitmap wbmap = new &#xA;      WriteableBitmap(100, 100, 300,&#xA;       300, PixelFormats.Bgra32, null);&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>This specifies a WriteableBitmap 100 by 100 pixels with a resolution of 300dpi by 300 dpi using a Bgra32 pixel format. Each pixel, a 32-bit int, uses a four-byte BGRA  that is the pixel is made up of a byte giving the Blue, Green, Red and Alpha values. The final parameter is used to specify a palette if the format needs one.&#xA;You can specify a wide range of formats for the bitmap you create and in each case each pixel takes a given number of bits to represent and you need to find out how the bits allocated to each pixel determine its colour.&#xA;The second method of creating a WriteableBitmap is to base it on an existing BitmapSource or derived class.  For example, you should be able to create a WriteableBitmap from a standard bitmap using the constructor:&#xA;   WriteableBitmap(bitmapsource);&#xA;but if you try this with a BitmapImage loaded from a URI you will   get a null object error. The reason is that the bitmap might not yet be downloaded. For a local file the bitmap load blocks execution until it is loaded:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code> Uri uri = new Uri(@"pack://application:&#xA;       ,,,/Resources/mypic.jpg");&#xA; BitmapImage bmi = new BitmapImage(uri);&#xA; WriteableBitmap bmi2 = new&#xA;            WriteableBitmap(bmi);&#xA; image1.Source = bmi2;&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>In this case the WriteableBitmap is created with no problems. If the URI was an HTTP URL, however, the load would not block the execution and the result would be an error.</p>&#xA;

pyrex	<p>Pyrex allows the user to write extension modules in a Python-like language which may directly access the external C code. The similarity of Pyrex's syntax to Python's makes it easy to write Python modules, as there is no need to learn another language (such as C or C++), and there may be no need to write any glue code. All that is needed is to specify the name of C-header files, enumerations, datatypes and functions needing to be accessed in the module, then simply use them as if they were Python objects. The Pyrex compiler will generate the necessary glue code automatically and compile the Pyrex code into a working Python module.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><a href="http://www.cosc.canterbury.ac.nz/greg.ewing/python/Pyrex/" rel="nofollow">Official Website</a></p>&#xA;

fixed-width	<p>Fixed layouts are layouts that start with a specific size, determined by the Web designer. They remain that width, regardless of the size of the browser window viewing the page. Fixed width layouts allow a designer more direct control over how the page will look in most situations. They are often preferred by designers with a print background, as they allow the designer to make minute adjustments to the layout and have them remain consistent across browsers and computers.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>source: <a href="http://webdesign.about.com/od/layout/g/bldeffixedlyot.htm" rel="nofollow">http://webdesign.about.com/od/layout/g/bldeffixedlyot.htm</a></p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Fixed Width Text File Definition: Above all, a fixed width text file is a file that has a specific format which allows for the saving of textual information/data in an organized fashion. &#xA;Fixed width text files are special cases of text files where the format is specified by column widths, pad character and left/right alignment.  Column widths are in units of characters. So if you have data in a text file where the first column always has exactly 10 characters, and the second column has exactly 5, the third has exactly 12 (and so on), then you have a fixed width text file.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Each row (paragraph) contains one record of information; each record can contain multiple pieces of data (fields), each data field (column) has a precise number of characters.  The data is padded with spaces (or any character you specify) if it does not completely use all the characters allotted to it. Further, each piece of data can be left or right justified, meaning the padding of characters can occur on either side.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>source: <a href="http://www.softinterface.com/Convert-XLS%5CFeatures%5CFixed-Width-Text-File-Definition.htm" rel="nofollow">http://www.softinterface.com/Convert-XLS%5CFeatures%5CFixed-Width-Text-File-Definition.htm</a></p>&#xA;

markov-models	<h2>Markov chain</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The simplest Markov model is the Markov chain. It models the state of a system with a random variable that changes through time. In this context, the Markov property suggests that the distribution for this variable depends only on the distribution of the previous state. An example use of a Markov chain is Markov Chain Monte Carlo, which uses the Markov property to prove that a particular method for performing a random walk will sample from the joint distribution of a system.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<h2>Hidden Markov model</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<p>A hidden Markov model is a Markov chain for which the state is only partially observable. In other words, observations are related to the state of the system, but they are typically insufficient to precisely determine the state. Several well-known algorithms for hidden Markov models exist. For example, given a sequence of observations, the Viterbi algorithm will compute the most-likely corresponding sequence of states, the forward algorithm will compute the probability of the sequence of observations, and the BaumWelch algorithm will estimate the starting probabilities, the transition function, and the observation function of a hidden Markov model.&#xA;One common use is for speech recognition, where the observed data is the speech audio waveform and the hidden state is the spoken text. In this example, the Viterbi algorithm finds the most likely sequence of spoken words given the speech audio.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<h2>Markov decision process</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<p>A Markov decision process is a Markov chain in which state transitions depend on the current state and an action vector that is applied to the system. Typically, a Markov decision process is used to compute a policy of actions that will maximize some utility with respect to expected rewards. It is closely related to Reinforcement learning, and can be solved with value iteration and related methods.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<h2>Partially observable Markov decision process</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<p>A partially observable Markov decision process (POMDP) is a Markov decision process in which the state of the system is only partially observed. POMDPs are known to be NP complete, but recent approximation techniques have made them useful for a variety of applications, such as controlling simple agents or robots.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<h2>Markov random field</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<p>A Markov random field, or Markov network, may be considered to be a generalization of a Markov chain in multiple dimensions. In a Markov chain, state depends only on the previous state in time, whereas in a Markov random field, each state depends on its neighbors in any of multiple directions. A Markov random field may be visualized as a field or graph of random variables, where the distribution of each random variable depends on the neighboring variables with which it is connected. More specifically, the joint distribution for any random variable in the graph can be computed as the product of the "clique potentials" of all the cliques in the graph that contain that random variable. Modeling a problem as a Markov random field is useful because it implies that the joint distributions at each vertex in the graph may be computed in this manner.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<h2>Hierarchical Markov Models</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Hierarchical Markov Models can be applied to categorize human behavior at various levels of abstraction. For example, a series of simple observations, such as a person's location in a room, can be interpreted to determine more complex information, such as in what task or activity the person is performing. Two kinds of Hierarchical Markov Models are the Hierarchical hidden Markov model and the Abstract Hidden Markov Model. Both have been used for behavior recognition, and certain conditional independence properties between different levels of abstraction in the model allow for faster learning and inference.</p>&#xA;
spread	<p>Some of the features are:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ol>&#xA;<li>Powerful Formula Engine with 300+ Excel Functions</li>&#xA;<li>Full Excel Import/Export, PDF, and Print </li>&#xA;<li>Support Input, Display, and Data Visualization Controls</li>&#xA;<li>Visual Drag-and-Drop Designers</li>&#xA;</ol>&#xA;

function-module	<p>Function modules allow you to encapsulate and reuse global functions in the SAP System. They are managed in a central function library. The SAP System contains several predefined functions modules that can be called from any ABAP program. Function modules also play an important role during updating  and in interaction between different SAP systems, or between SAP systems and remote systems through remote communications.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Unlike subroutines, you do not define function modules in the source code of your program. Instead, you use the Function Builder. The actual ABAP interface definition remains hidden from the programmer. You can define the input parameters of a function module as optional. You can also assign default values to them. Function modules also support exception handling. This allows you to catch certain errors while the function module is running. You can test function modules without having to include them in a program using the Function Builder.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The Function Builder  also has a release process for function modules. This ensures that incompatible changes cannot be made to any function modules that have already been released. This applies particularly to the interface. Programs that use a released function module will not cease to work if the function module is changed.</p>&#xA;
html-parser	<p>HTML Parser is a Java HTML parsing library. It features filters, visitors, custom tags and easy to use JavaBeans.</p>&#xA;

The clip bounds and CTM of the drawing context can be used to determine the bounds and resolution of the tile being requested.</p>&#xA;

viewstub	<p>A ViewStub is an invisible, zero-sized View that can be used to lazily inflate layout resources at runtime. When a ViewStub is made visible, or when inflate() is invoked, the layout resource is inflated. The ViewStub then replaces itself in its parent with the inflated View or Views. Therefore, the ViewStub exists in the view hierarchy until setVisibility(int) or inflate() is invoked. The inflated View is added to the ViewStub's parent with the ViewStub's layout parameters. conversation-scope	<p>The conversation scope is a bit like the traditional session scope in that it holds state associated with a user of the system, and spans multiple requests to the server. However, unlike the session scope, the conversation scope:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li><p>is demarcated explicitly by the application, and</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>holds state associated with a particular web browser tab in a JSF application (browsers tend to share domain cookies, and hence the session cookie, between tabs, so this is not the case for the session scope). </p></li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;&#xA;<p>A conversation represents a taska unit of work from the point of view of the user. The conversation context holds state associated with what the user is currently working on. If the user is doing multiple things at the same time, there are multiple conversations.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The conversation context is active during any JSF request. Most conversations are destroyed at the end of the request. If a conversation should hold state across multiple requests, it must be explicitly promoted to a long-running conversation. </p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>For more about it : <a href="https://docs.jboss.org/weld/reference/1.0.1-Final/en-US/html/scopescontexts.html" rel="nofollow">https://docs.jboss.org/weld/reference/1.0.1-Final/en-US/html/scopescontexts.html</a> </p>&#xA;

Google Merchant Center is where your product feed lives. Well get into the details of your feed momentarily, but in a nutshell, its the details of your products organized in a format Google likes. AdWords is where your actual shopping campaigns live and where youll set your budget, manage your bids, gain insights, and make optimizations based on performance.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The setup and management of Google Shopping ads is quite a bit different from setting up traditional text ads. benfords-law	<p>Benford's law states that in lists of numbers from many (but not all) real-life sources of data, the leading digit is distributed in a specific, non-uniform way. According to this law, the first digit is 1 about 30% of the time, and larger digits occur as the leading digit with lower and lower frequency, to the point where 9 as a first digit occurs less than 5% of the time. This distribution of first digits is the same as the widths of gridlines on the logarithmic scale.</p>&#xA;

static-memory-allocation	<p>In computer programming, a static variable is a variable that has been allocated statically so that its lifetime or "extent" extends across the entire run of the program. This is in contrast to the more ephemeral automatic variables (local variables are generally automatic), whose storage is allocated and deallocated on the call stack; and in contrast to objects whose storage is dynamically allocated in heap memory. Static memory allocation in general is the allocation of memory at compile time before the associated program is executed, unlike dynamic memory allocation or automatic memory allocation where memory is allocated as required at run time.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The absolute address addressing mode can only be used with static variables, because those are the only kinds of variables whose location is known by the compiler at compile time. When the program (executable or library) is loaded into memory, static variables are stored in the data segment of the program's address space (if initialized), or the BSS segment (if uninitialized), and are stored in corresponding sections of object files prior to loading.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The static keyword is used in C and related languages both for static variables and other concepts.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Source: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Static_variable" rel="nofollow">Wikipedia</a></p>&#xA;

wcf-data-services-client	<p>Any application can interact with an Open Data Protocol (OData)-based data service if it can send an HTTP request and process the OData feed that a data service returns. This interoperability enables you to access OData-based services from a broad range of Web-enabled applications. WCF Data Services includes client libraries that provide a richer programming experience when you consume OData feeds from .NET Framework or Silverlight-based applications.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The two main classes of the client library are the DataServiceContext class and the DataServiceQuery class. The DataServiceContext class encapsulates operations that are supported against a specified data service. Although OData services are stateless, the context is not. Therefore, you can use the DataServiceContext class to maintain state on the client between interactions with the data service in order to support features such as change management. This class also manages identities and tracks changes. The DataServiceQuery class represents a query against a specific entity set.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>This section describes how to use client libraries to access and change data from a .NET Framework client application. For more information about how to use the WCF Data Services client library with a Silverlight-based application, see WCF Data Services (Silverlight). Other client libraries are available that enable you to consume an OData feed in other kinds of applications. For more information, see the OData SDK.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Read more in the <a href="https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/cc668772(v=vs.110).aspx" rel="nofollow">ref</a>.</p>&#xA;

spring-validator	<p>The Core package is the most fundamental part of the framework and provides the IoC and Dependency Injection features. The basic concept here is the BeanFactory, which provides a sophisticated implementation of the factory pattern which removes the need for programmatic singletons and allows you to decouple the configuration and specification of dependencies from your actual program logic.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The Context package build on the solid base provided by the Core package: it provides a way to access objects in a framework-style manner in a fashion somewhat reminiscent of a JNDI-registry. The context package inherits its features from the beans package and adds support for internationalization (I18N) (using for example resource bundles), event-propagation, resource-loading, and the transparent creation of contexts by, for example, a servlet container.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The DAO package provides a JDBC-abstraction layer that removes the need to do tedious JDBC coding and parsing of database-vendor specific error codes. Also, the JDBC package provides a way to do programmatic as well as declarative transaction management, not only for classes implementing special interfaces, but for all your POJOs (plain old Java objects).</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The ORM package provides integration layers for popular object-relational mapping APIs, including JPA, JDO, Hibernate, and iBatis. Using the ORM package you can use all those O/R-mappers in combination with all the other features Spring offers, such as the simple declarative transaction management feature mentioned previously.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Spring's AOP package provides an AOP Alliance-compliant aspect-oriented programming implementation allowing you to define, for example, method-interceptors and pointcuts to cleanly decouple code implementing functionality that should logically speaking be separated. Using source-level metadata functionality you can also incorporate all kinds of behavioral information into your code, in a manner similar to that of .NET attributes.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Spring's Web package provides basic web-oriented integration features, such as multipart file-upload functionality, the initialization of the IoC container using servlet listeners and a web-oriented application context. When using Spring together with WebWork or Struts, this is the package to integrate with.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Spring's MVC package provides a Model-View-Controller (MVC) implementation for web-applications. Spring's MVC framework is not just any old implementation; it provides a clean separation between domain model code and web forms, and allows you to use all the other features of the Spring Framework.</p>&#xA;

If handle animation is enabled, the handle slides to the specified point on the rail with a nice animation effect. </p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>When a value is chosen using the Slider, it is automatically persisted during full or partial postbacks. The developer can continue to reference the asp:TextBox to get and set the Slider's value. </p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The Slider's value can be dynamically displayed in another asp:TextBox or an asp:Label. If a TextBox is used, the Slider's value can be updated through the bound TextBox. </p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>By declaring the extended TextBox as a trigger for an UpdatePanel, the Slider can fire the update whenever the handle is released. By setting the RaiseChangeOnlyOnMouseUp to false, the update will be fired as soon as the Slider's value changes. </p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The TooltipText property allows to display some text when the mouse pointer hovers the slider's handle. A {0} placeholder in the text is replaced by the current value of the slider.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><a href="http://www.asp.net/ajaxLibrary/AjaxControlToolkitSampleSite/Slider/Slider.aspx" rel="nofollow">More Details...</a></p>&#xA;

forward-indexing	<p>The forward index stores a list of words for each document.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The rationale behind developing a forward index is that as documents are parsing, it is better to immediately store the words per document. The delineation enables Asynchronous system processing, which partially circumvents the inverted index update bottleneck.[18] The forward index is sorted to transform it to an inverted index. The forward index is essentially a list of pairs consisting of a document and a word, collated by the document. Converting the forward index to an inverted index is only a matter of sorting the pairs by the words. In this regard, the inverted index is a word-sorted forward index.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_engine_indexing#The_forward_index" rel="nofollow">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_engine_indexing#The_forward_index</a></p>&#xA;

It provides the following classes that define time in the calendar system based on the International Organization for Standardization (ISO) calendar.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li><p>Clock  a clock providing access to the current instant, date, and time using a time-zone</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>Duration  a time-based amount of time</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>Instant  an instantaneous point on the timeline</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>LocalDate  a date without a time-zone in the ISO-8601 calendar system</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>LocalDateTime  a date-time without a time zone in the ISO-8601 calendar system</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>LocalTime  a time without time zone in the ISO-8601 calendar system</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>MonthDay  a month day in the ISO-8601 calendar system</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>OffsetDateTime  a date-time with an offset from Greenwich/UTC time in the ISO-8601 calendar system</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>OffsetTime  a time with an offset from Greenwich/UTC time in the ISO-8601 calendar system</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>Period  a date-based amount of time</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>Year  a year in the ISO-8601 calendar system</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>YearMonth  a year-month in the ISO-8601 calendar system</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>ZonedDateTime  a date time with a time zone in the ISO-8601 calendar system</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>ZoneId  a time zone ID</p></li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;&#xA;<p>-ZoneOffset  a time zone offset from Greenwich/UTC time</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><em>See the Date-Time API trail of the Java Tutorials for more information about the available functionality and code samples.</em></p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/javase/8/javafx/user-interface-tutorial/date-picker.htm" rel="nofollow">Source</a></p>&#xA;

angularjs-sce	<p>Strict Contextual Escaping (SCE) is a mode in which AngularJS requires bindings in certain contexts to result in a value that is marked as safe to use for that context. One example of such a context is binding arbitrary html controlled by the user via ng-bind-html. We refer to these contexts as privileged or SCE contexts.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>As of version 1.2, Angular ships with SCE enabled by default.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Note: When enabled (the default), IE&lt;11 in quirks mode is not supported. In this mode, IE&lt;11 allow one to execute arbitrary javascript by the use of the expression() syntax. Refer to learn more about them. You can ensure your document is in standards mode and not quirks mode by adding  to the top of your HTML document.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>SCE assists in writing code in way that (a) is secure by default and (b) makes auditing for security vulnerabilities such as XSS, clickjacking, etc. a lot easier.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Here's an example of a binding in a privileged context:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>&lt;input ng-model="userHtml" aria-label="User input"&gt;&#xA;&lt;div ng-bind-html="userHtml"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Notice that ng-bind-html is bound to userHtml controlled by the user. With SCE disabled, this application allows the user to render arbitrary HTML into the DIV. In a more realistic example, one may be rendering user comments, blog articles, etc. via bindings. (HTML is just one example of a context where rendering user controlled input creates security vulnerabilities.)</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>For the case of HTML, you might use a library, either on the client side, or on the server side, to sanitize unsafe HTML before binding to the value and rendering it in the document.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>How would you ensure that every place that used these types of bindings was bound to a value that was sanitized by your library (or returned as safe for rendering by your server?) How can you ensure that you didn't accidentally delete the line that sanitized the value, or renamed some properties/fields and forgot to update the binding to the sanitized value?</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>To be secure by default, you want to ensure that any such bindings are disallowed unless you can determine that something explicitly says it's safe to use a value for binding in that context. You can then audit your code (a simple grep would do) to ensure that this is only done for those values that you can easily tell are safe - because they were received from your server, sanitized by your library, etc. You can organize your codebase to help with this - perhaps allowing only the files in a specific directory to do this. Ensuring that the internal API exposed by that code doesn't markup arbitrary values as safe then becomes a more manageable task.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>In the case of AngularJS' SCE service, one uses $sce.trustAs (and shorthand methods such as $sce.trustAsHtml, etc.) to obtain values that will be accepted by SCE / privileged contexts.</p>&#xA;

javascript-oscillator	<p>In molecular biology, an oscillating gene is a gene that is expressed in a rhythmic pattern or in periodic cycles.[1][2] Oscillating genes are usually circadian and can be identified by periodic changes in the state of an organism. Circadian rhythms, controlled by oscillating genes, have a period of approximately 24 hours. For example, plant leaves opening and closing at different times of the day or the sleep-wake schedule of animals can all include circadian rhythms. Other periods are also possible, such as 29.5 days resulting from circalunar rhythms or 12.4 hours resulting from circatidal rhythms.[3] Oscillating genes include both core clock component genes and output genes. A core clock component gene is a gene necessary for to the pacemaker. However, an output oscillating gene, such as the AVP gene, is rhythmic but not necessary to the pacemaker.[4]</p>&#xA;

injective-function	<p>In mathematics, an <strong>injective function</strong> or <strong>injection</strong> or <strong>one-to-one function</strong> is a function that preserves distinctness: it never maps distinct elements of its domain to the same element of its codomain. In other words, every element of the function's codomain is the image of at most one element of its domain. The term one-to-one function must not be confused with one-to-one correspondence (a.k.a. bijective function), which uniquely maps all elements in both domain and codomain to each other</p>&#xA;&#xA;<h3>Source:</h3>&#xA;&#xA;<p><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Injective_function" rel="nofollow noreferrer">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Injective_function</a></p>&#xA;

android-layoutparams	<p>The base LayoutParams class just describes how big the view wants to be for both width and height. For each dimension, it can specify one of:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li><code>FILL_PARENT</code> (renamed <code>MATCH_PARENT</code> in API Level 8 and higher), which means that the view wants to be as big as its parent (minus padding)</li>&#xA;<li><code>WRAP_CONTENT</code>, which means that the view wants to be just big enough to enclose its content (plus padding)&#xA;an exact number</li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;&#xA;<p>There are subclasses of LayoutParams for different subclasses of ViewGroup. For example, AbsoluteLayout has its own subclass of LayoutParams which adds an X and Y value.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<h2>Useful links</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.LayoutParams.html" rel="nofollow">Official reference</a></li>&#xA;<li><a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/ui/declaring-layout.html" rel="nofollow">XML layouts - official developer guide</a></li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;

django-activity-stream	<p><a href="https://github.com/justquick/django-activity-stream" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Django Activity Stream</a> is a module to generate JSON feeds of activities such as "justquick (actor) closed (verb) issue 2 (object) on django-activity-stream (target) 12 hours ago" in <a href="http://activitystrea.ms/" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Activity Streams</a> format. </p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Here is a simple, minimal example of a JSON serialized activity:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre class="lang-json prettyprint-override"><code>  {&#xA;    "published": "2011-02-10T15:04:55Z",&#xA;    "actor": {&#xA;      "url": "http://example.org/martin",&#xA;      "objectType" : "person",&#xA;      "id": "tag:example.org,2011:martin",&#xA;      "image": {&#xA;        "url": "http://example.org/martin/image",&#xA;        "width": 250,&#xA;        "height": 250&#xA;      },&#xA;      "displayName": "Martin Smith"&#xA;    },&#xA;    "verb": "post",&#xA;    "object" : {&#xA;      "url": "http://example.org/blog/2011/02/entry",&#xA;      "id": "tag:example.org,2011:abc123/xyz"&#xA;    },&#xA;    "target" : {&#xA;      "url": "http://example.org/blog/",&#xA;      "objectType": "blog",&#xA;      "id": "tag:example.org,2011:abc123",&#xA;      "displayName": "Martin's Blog"&#xA;    }&#xA;  }&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>A single activity consists of an <code>actor</code> (required), a <code>verb</code> (required), an an <code>object</code> (optional), and a <code>target</code> (optional). In Django Activity Stream each of those noun components might be any properly registered Django Model. </p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>There are some pre-defined streams such as User streams (what the given user did) or Target streams (what happened to the given target) and you can create your own custom ones.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>GitHub with the source is located at <a href="https://github.com/justquick/django-activity-stream" rel="nofollow noreferrer">https://github.com/justquick/django-activity-stream</a> and official documentation is at <a href="http://django-activity-stream.readthedocs.io/en/latest/" rel="nofollow noreferrer">http://django-activity-stream.readthedocs.io/en/latest/</a></p>&#xA;

auryn	<p>Auryn is used to bootstrap and wire together S.O.L.I.D., object-oriented PHP applications.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<blockquote>&#xA;  <p><strong>How It Works:</strong>&#xA;  Among other things, auryn recursively instantiates class dependencies based on the parameter type-hints specified in class constructor signatures. This requires the use of Reflection. You may have heard that "reflection is slow". Let's clear something up: anything can be "slow" if you're doing it wrong. Reflection is an order of magnitude faster than disk access and several orders of magnitude faster than retrieving information (for example) from a remote database. Additionally, each reflection offers the opportunity to cache the results if you're worried about speed. auryn caches any reflections it generates to minimize the potential performance impact.</p>&#xA;  &#xA;  <p><strong>Requirements :</strong> auryn requires PHP 5.3 or higher.</p>&#xA;</blockquote>&#xA;&#xA;<p>For more information take a look at the repository <a href="https://github.com/rdlowrey/Auryn" rel="nofollow">auryn</a> </p>&#xA;

android-percent-layout	<p><strong>As Android Document says</strong>&#xA;Subclass of <a href="http://developer.android.com/reference/android/widget/RelativeLayout.html" rel="nofollow">RelativeLayout</a> that supports percentage based dimensions and margins. You can specify dimension or a margin of child by using attributes with "Percent" suffix.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>It is not necessary to specify <strong>layout_width/height</strong> if you specify <strong>layout_widthPercent</strong>. However, if you want the view to be able to take up more space than what percentage value permits, you can add <strong>layout_width/height="wrap_content"</strong>. In that case if the percentage size is too small for the View's content, it will be resized using <strong>wrap_content</strong> rule.</p>&#xA;

backupmanager	<p>When an application has made changes to data which should be backed up, a call to <a href="http://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/backup/BackupManager.html#dataChanged()" rel="nofollow">dataChanged()</a> will notify the backup service. The system will then schedule a backup operation to occur in the near future. Repeated calls to <a href="http://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/backup/BackupManager.html#dataChanged()" rel="nofollow">dataChanged()</a> have no further effect until the backup operation actually occurs.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>A backup or restore operation for your application begins when the system launches the <a href="http://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/backup/BackupAgent.html" rel="nofollow">BackupAgent</a> subclass you've declared in your manifest. See the documentation for <a href="http://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/backup/BackupAgent.html" rel="nofollow">BackupAgent</a> for a detailed description of how the operation then proceeds.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Several attributes affecting the operation of the backup and restore mechanism can be set on the <a href="http://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/application-element.html" rel="nofollow"></a> tag in your application's AndroidManifest.xml file.</p>&#xA;

hybrid-cloud	<p>A hybrid cloud is an integrated cloud service utilising both private and public clouds to perform distinct functions within the same organisation. All cloud computing services should offer certain efficiencies to differing degrees but public cloud services are likely to be more cost efficient and scalable than private clouds. Therefore, an organisation can maximise their efficiencies by employing public cloud services for all non-sensitive operations, only relying on a private cloud where they require it and ensuring that all of their platforms are seamlessly integrated.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Hybrid cloud models can be implemented in a number of ways:&#xA;Separate cloud providers team up to provide both private and public services as an integrated service&#xA;Individual cloud providers offer a complete hybrid package&#xA;Organisations who manage their private clouds themselves sign up to a public cloud service which they then integrate into their infrastructure</p>&#xA;

To complement these functions <code>ggplot()</code> methods for <code>"ts"</code> and <code>"xts"</code> classes are also defined.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Different <em>statistics</em>, <em>geometries</em> and functions add facilities for labelling peaks and valleys, generating labels for fitted models including polynomial equations, highlighting deviations from a model fit, and for filtering-out regions of plot panels with high densities of observations (with stats designed to work nicely together with R package 'ggrepel').</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Another group of ggplot statistics and geometries which echo their input to the R console aim at easing debugging during development of new 'ggplot2' <em>geometries</em> and <em>statistics</em> (or learning how they work).</p>&#xA;

sslcontext	<p>According to <a href="http://www.ibm.com/support/knowledgecenter/SSYKE2_6.0.0/com.ibm.java.security.component.60.doc/security-component/jsse2Docs/sslcontext.html" rel="nofollow">IBM Knowledge Center</a>,</p>&#xA;&#xA;<blockquote>&#xA;  <p>The SSLContext is an engine class for an implementation of a secure&#xA;  socket protocol. An instance of this class acts as a factory for SSL&#xA;  socket factories and SSL engines. An SSLContext holds all of the state&#xA;  information shared across all objects created under that context. For&#xA;  example, session state is associated with the SSLContext when it is&#xA;  negotiated through the handshake protocol by sockets created by socket&#xA;  factories provided by the context. These cached sessions can be reused&#xA;  and shared by other sockets created under the same context.</p>&#xA;  &#xA;  <p>Each instance is configured through its init method with the keys,&#xA;  certificate chains, and trusted root CA certificates that it needs to&#xA;  perform authentication. This configuration is provided in the form of&#xA;  key and trust managers. These managers provide support for the&#xA;  authentication and key agreement aspects of the cipher suites&#xA;  supported by the context.</p>&#xA;</blockquote>&#xA;

pedometer	<p>A pedometer is a device, usually portable and electronic or electromechanical, that counts each step a person takes by detecting the motion of the person's hands or hips. Because the distance of each person's step varies, an informal calibration, performed by the user, is required if presentation of the distance covered in a unit of length (such as in kilometers or miles) is desired, though there are now pedometers that use electronics and software to automatically determine how a person's step varies. Distance traveled (by walking or any other means) can be measured directly by a GPS tracker.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Used originally by sports and physical fitness enthusiasts, pedometers are now becoming popular as an everyday exercise counter and motivator. Often worn on the belt and kept on all day, it can record how many steps the wearer has walked that day, and thus the kilometers or miles (distance = number of steps × step length). Some pedometers will also erroneously record movements other than walking, such as bending to tie one's shoes, or road bumps incurred while riding a vehicle, though the most advanced devices record fewer of these 'false steps'. Step counters can give encouragement to compete with oneself in getting fit and losing weight. A total of 10,000 steps per day, equivalent to 8 kilometres (5.0 mi), is recommended by some to be the benchmark for an active lifestyle, although this point is debated among experts. Thirty minutes of moderate walking are equivalent to 3,000-4,000 steps as determined by a pedometer. Step counters are being integrated into an increasing number of portable consumer electronic devices such as music players, smartphones, and mobile phones.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>From Wikipedia: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pedometer" rel="nofollow">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pedometer</a></p>&#xA;

yarp	<p>More specifically, YARP supports building a robot control system as a collection of programs communicating in a peer-to-peer way, with an extensible family of connection types (tcp, udp, multicast, local, MPI, mjpg-over-http, XML/RPC, tcpros, ...) that can be swapped in and out to match your needs. We also support similarly flexible interfacing with hardware devices. Our strategic goal is to increase the longevity of robot software projects.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>YARP is not an operating system for your robot. We figure you already have an operating system, or perhaps several. Nor does it do package management (we like the package managers we have). We're not out for world domination. It is easy to interoperate with YARP-using programs without yourself necessarily having to use YARP codebase  see the YARP without YARP tutorial. YARP is written in C++. The ACE library is used for Windows builds, and to support extra protocols. On Linux and Mac OSX, ACE can optionally be omitted, giving a very light footprint (with the trade-off being the loss of support for some non-TCP-based protocols). YARP is free and open, under the LGPL (*).</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><a href="http://www.yarp.it/index.html" rel="nofollow">http://www.yarp.it/index.html</a></p>&#xA;

dart-dev-compiler	<p>The Dart Dev Compiler (DDC) is a development tool and transpiler. It is at a very early stage today. Its aims include the following:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li>A static checker based on stricter-than-standard-Dart type rules.</li>&#xA;<li>A modular Dart-to-ES6 transpiler for Dart programs that statically check.</li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;&#xA;<p>DDC attempts to map to idiomatic EcmaScript 6 (ES6) as cleanly as possible. To do this while cohering to Dart semantics, DDC relies heavily on static type information, static checking, and runtime assertions.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>DDC is intended to support a very large subset of Dart. If a program does not statically check, DDC will not result in valid generated code. Our goal is that a program execution (of a valid program) that runs without triggering runtime assertions should run the same on other Dart platforms under checked mode or production mode.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>DDC does support untyped Dart code, but it will typically result in less readable and less efficient ES6 output.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>DDC has the following project goals:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li>Effective static checking and error detection.</li>&#xA;<li>A debugging solution for all modern browsers.</li>&#xA;<li>Readable output.</li>&#xA;<li>Fast, modular compilation of Dart code.</li>&#xA;<li>Easy use of generated code from JavaScript.</li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;&#xA;<p>DDC is targeting the subset of ES6 supported in Chrome.</p>&#xA;

The advantage of this is that Ajax-patterned&#xA;applications can handle JSON formatted data without having to rely on&#xA;ActiveX objects in Microsoft Internet Explorer XML transformations&#xA;and other platform-specific XML parsers.  In addition, JSON-formatted&#xA;data tends to be more compact and efficient to transfer.</li>&#xA;<li>A JSON string and stream parser that can generate the corresponding&#xA;JSONObject, which represents that JSON structure in Java. amazon-s3-infrequent	<p>Amazon S3 Standard - Infrequent Access (Standard - IA) is an Amazon S3 storage class for data that is accessed less frequently but requires rapid access when needed. Standard - IA offers the high durability, throughput, and low latency of Amazon S3 Standard, with a low per GB storage price and per GB retrieval fee. This combination of low cost and high performance make Standard - IA ideal for long-term storage, backups, and as a data store for disaster recovery. The Standard - IA storage class is set at the object level and can exist in the same bucket as Standard, allowing you to use lifecycle policies to automatically transition objects between storage classes without any application changes.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/s3/storage-classes/" rel="nofollow">https://aws.amazon.com/s3/storage-classes/</a></p>&#xA;

pybind11	<h1>pybind11  Seamless operability between C++11 and Python.</h1>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The following core C++ features can be mapped to Python:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li>Functions accepting and returning custom data structures per value, reference, or pointer</li>&#xA;<li>Instance methods and static methods</li>&#xA;<li>Overloaded functions</li>&#xA;<li>Instance attributes and static attributes</li>&#xA;<li>Many more</li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;&#xA;<p>In addition to the core functionality, pybind11 provides some extra goodies:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li>Python 2.7, 3.x, and PyPy (PyPy2.7 >= 5.7) are supported with an implementation-agnostic interface.</li>&#xA;<li>It is possible to bind C++11 lambda functions with captured variables. The lambda capture data is stored inside the resulting Python function object.</li>&#xA;<li>pybind11 uses C++11 move constructors and move assignment operators whenever possible to efficiently transfer custom data types.</li>&#xA;<li>Still more</li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Supported compilers:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li>Clang/LLVM (any non-ancient version with C++11 support)</li>&#xA;<li>GCC 4.8 or newer</li>&#xA;<li>Microsoft Visual Studio 2015 or newer</li>&#xA;<li>Intel C++ compiler v15 or newer</li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;&#xA;<p>See documentation at <a href="https://pybind11.readthedocs.io/en/latest/index.html" rel="nofollow noreferrer">https://pybind11.readthedocs.io/en/latest/index.html</a></p>&#xA;
tx-fluidcontent	<p>It is available through the <a href="https://typo3.org/extensions/repository/view/fluidcontent" rel="nofollow">TER</a> and <a href="https://github.com/FluidTYPO3/fluidcontent" rel="nofollow">GitHub</a></p>&#xA;&#xA;<h2>What does it do?</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<p>EXT:fluidcontent lets you write custom content elements based on Fluid templates. Each content element and its possible settings&#xA;are contained in a single Fluid template file. Whole sets of files can be registered and placed in its own tab in the new content&#xA;element wizard, letting you group your content elements. The template files are placed in a very basic extension. The <em>Nested&#xA;Content Elements</em> support that Flux enables is utilized to make content elements which can contain other content elements.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<h2>Why use it?</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<p><strong>Fluid Content</strong> is a fast, dynamic and extremely flexible way to create content elements. Not only can you use Fluid, you can&#xA;also create dynamic configuration options for each content element using Flux - in the exact same way as done in the Fluid Pages&#xA;extension; see <a href="https://github.com/FluidTYPO3/fluidpages" rel="nofollow">https://github.com/FluidTYPO3/fluidpages</a>.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<h2>How does it work?</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Fluid Content Elements are registered through TypoScript. The template files are then processed to read various information about&#xA;each template, which is then made available for use just as any other content element type is used.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>When editing the content element, Flux is used to generate the form section which lets content editors configure variables which&#xA;become available in the template. This allows completely dynamic variables (as opposed to adding extra fields on the <code>tt_content</code>&#xA;table and configuring TCA for each added column).</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>View the <a href="https://fluidtypo3.org/documentation/templating-manual/introduction.html" rel="nofollow">online templating manual</a> for more information.</p>&#xA;

Built on the cross-platform <a href="https://realm.io/products/realm-mobile-database/" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Realm Mobile Database</a>, it supports both iOS and Android, and the Realm Object Server is ready to run on your servers or on your favorite cloud.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Questions about Realm Mobile Platform, Realm Object Server, or data synchronization using Realm should use this tag. open-components	<h1><img src="https://raw.github.com/opentable/oc/master/logo.png" alt="oc"></h1>&#xA;&#xA;<p>OpenComponents, <strong>serverless in the front-end world</strong>.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>OpenComponents is an open-source framework that allows fast-moving teams to easily build and deploy front-end components. It abstracts away complicated infrastructure and leaves developers with very simple, but powerful building blocks that handle scale transparently.</p>&#xA;&#xA;How does it work?&#xA;&#xA;<p>First, <strong>you create your component</strong>. It can contain logic to get some data (using node.js) and then the view, including css and js. It can be what you want, including <em>React</em> or <em>Angular</em> components or whatever you like.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Then, <strong>you publish it</strong> to the OpenComponents registry and you wait a couple of seconds while the registry prepares your stuff to be production-ready.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Now, every web app in your private or public network can <strong>consume the component</strong> via its own HTTP endpoint during server-side rendering or just in the browser.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>We have been using for more than a year in production at OpenTable, for shared components, third party widgets, and more. <a href="http://tech.opentable.co.uk/blog/2016/04/27/opencomponents-microservices-in-the-front-end-world/" rel="nofollow">Learn more about OC</a>.</p>&#xA;

livy	<p>From <a href="http://livy.incubator.apache.org" rel="nofollow noreferrer">http://livy.incubator.apache.org</a>.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<blockquote>&#xA;  <h1>What is Apache Livy?</h1>&#xA;  &#xA;  <p>Apache Livy is a service that enables easy interaction with a Spark cluster over a REST interface. It enables easy submission of Spark jobs or snippets of Spark code, synchronous or asynchronous result retrieval, as well as Spark Context management, all via a simple REST interface or a RPC client library. Apache Livy also simplifies the interaction between Spark from application servers, thus enabling the use of Spark for interactive web/mobile applications. Additional features include:</p>&#xA;  &#xA;  <ul>&#xA;  <li>Have long running Spark Contexts that can be used for multiple Spark jobs, by multiple clients</li>&#xA;  <li>Share cached RDDs or Dataframes across multiple jobs and clients</li>&#xA;  <li>Multiple Spark Contexts can be managed simultaneously, and the Spark Contexts run on the cluster (YARN/Mesos) instead of the Livy Server, for good fault tolerance and concurrency</li>&#xA;  <li>Jobs can be submitted as precompiled jars, snippets of code or via java/scala client API</li>&#xA;  <li>Ensure security via secure authenticated communication</li>&#xA;  </ul>&#xA;</blockquote>&#xA;&#xA;<h2>References</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li><a href="http://livy.incubator.apache.org" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Project Home</a></li>&#xA;<li><a href="https://github.com/apache/incubator-livy" rel="nofollow noreferrer">GitHub</a></li>&#xA;<li><a href="http://livy.incubator.apache.org/download/" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Downloads</a></li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;

data-race	<p>A data race occurs when:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li><p>two or more threads in a single process access the same memory location concurrently, and</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>at least one of the accesses is for writing, and</p></li>&#xA;<li><p>the threads are not using any exclusive locks to control their accesses to that memory.</p></li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;&#xA;<p>When these three conditions hold, the order of accesses is non-deterministic, and the computation may give different results from run to run depending on that order. Some data-races may be benign (for example, when the memory access is used for a busy-wait), but many data-races are bugs in the program.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>(source: <a href="https://docs.oracle.com/cd/E19205-01/820-0619/geojs/index.html" rel="nofollow noreferrer">https://docs.oracle.com/cd/E19205-01/820-0619/geojs/index.html</a>)</p>&#xA;

Core tenets:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li>State is a single immutable data structure</li>&#xA;<li>Actions describe state changes</li>&#xA;<li>Pure functions called reducers take the previous state and the next action to compute the new state</li>&#xA;<li>State accessed with the <code>Store</code>, an observable of state and an observer of actions</li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;&#xA;<p>These core principles enable building components that can use the <code>OnPush</code> change detection strategy giving you intelligent, performance change detection throughout your application.</p>&#xA;

dgraph	<p><a href="https://dgraph.io/" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Dgraph</a> is an open source, scalable, distributed and highly available graph database. It's sharded storage and query processing were specifically designed to minimize the number of network calls. The database server and tools, written in <code>go</code>, are open-sourced and available under <a href="https://github.com/dgraph-io/dgraph/blob/master/GNU-AGPL-3.0.txt" rel="nofollow noreferrer">AGPL v3.0</a>.&#xA;The query language is named <code>GraphQL+-</code> and is based on <a href="http://graphql.org/" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Facebooks <code>GraphQL</code></a>. </p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The clients communicate with the server using <a href="https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Protocol Buffers</a> over <a href="https://grpc.io/" rel="nofollow noreferrer">gRPC</a>. &#xA;In the current version (v0.8.0), the available clients are limited to the languages Go, Python and Java, where Python and Java clients are marked as <em>Incomplete</em> due to insufficient resources and favoring development on the Go client.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Dgraph is still at an early state of development. The latest version, tagged v0.8.0, is still not stable enough to be used safely in a production environment. As a result, they suggest using the database only for internal applications while taking frequent <a href="https://docs.dgraph.io/deploy/#export" rel="nofollow noreferrer">exports</a>.&#xA;For more information check following FAQ topics:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li><a href="https://docs.dgraph.io/faq/#why-would-i-not-use-dgraph" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Why would I not use Dgraph?</a></li>&#xA;<li><a href="https://docs.dgraph.io/faq/#is-dgraph-production-ready" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Is Dgraph production ready?</a></li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;&#xA;<h2>Useful links</h2>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li><a href="https://docs.dgraph.io/master/get-started/#step-1-install-dgraph" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Dgraph Installation Guide</a></li>&#xA;<li><a href="https://docs.dgraph.io/query-language/" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Dgraph Query Language</a></li>&#xA;<li><a href="https://docs.dgraph.io/clients/" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Dgraph Client Drivers jdeprscan	<p><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/javase/9/tools/jdeprscan.htm#JSWOR-GUID-2B7588B0-92DB-4A88-88D4-24D183660A62" rel="nofollow noreferrer">jdeprscan</a> is a static analysis tool which can be used for scanning an aggregation of the class files in <a href="/questions/tagged/java" class="post-tag" title="show questions tagged &#39;java&#39;" rel="tag">java</a> for the use of deprecated API elements. Its usage is as :</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>jdeprscan [ options ]{dir|jar|class}&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Example of its usage is :</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>jdeprscan commons-math3-3.6.1.jar &#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>where one line of output might be:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<blockquote>&#xA;<pre><code>class org/apache/commons/math3/util/MathUtils uses deprecated method&#xA;java/lang/Double::&lt;init&gt;(D)V&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;</blockquote>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The name of the deprecated method is , which is a special name that means that the method is actually a constructor. Another special name is , which indicates a class static initializer. Other methods are just listed by their method name. Following the method name is the argument list and return type: <code>(D)V</code>. This indicates that it takes a single <code>double</code> value (a primitive) and returns <code>void</code></p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The argument and return types can become cryptic. For example, another line of output might be:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<blockquote>&#xA;<pre><code>class org/apache/commons/math3/util/Precision uses deprecated method&#xA;java/math/BigDecimal::setScale(II)Ljava/math/BigDecimal;&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;</blockquote>&#xA;&#xA;<p>In this line of output, the deprecated method is on class <code>java.math.BigDecimal</code>, and the method is <code>setScale()</code>. In this case, the <strong><code>(II)</code></strong> means that it takes two int arguments. The <strong><code>Ljava/math/BigDecimal;</code></strong> after the parentheses means that it returns a reference to <code>java.math.BigDecimal.</code></p>&#xA;
