grace-ioc	<p><a href="https://github.com/ipjohnson/Grace" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Grace on GitHub</a></p>&#xA;&#xA;<h1>Features in Grace</h1>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li>Fluent interface or Attributes for configuration allowing for maximum flexibility</li>&#xA;<li>Supports child containers and light weight lifetime scopes</li>&#xA;<li>Contextual binding support (similar to NInject)</li>&#xA;<li>IDisposable objects created by the container will be tracked and disposed by the container unless configured otherwise.</li>&#xA;<li>Performance characteristics that make it one of the fastest containers available. (<a href="http://www.palmmedia.de/blog/2011/8/30/ioc-container-benchmark-performance-comparison" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Benchmarks</a>)</li>&#xA;<li>Supports special types&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li>IEnumerable&lt;T&gt; - supports resolving collections as IEnumerable&lt;T&gt; as well as most other types of collections List&lt;T&gt;, ReadOnlyCollection&lt;T&gt;, T[] and any collection that implements ICollection&lt;T&gt;</li>&#xA;<li>Func&lt;T&gt; - supports resolving Func&#xA;<li>Lazy&lt;T&gt; - when resolved a Lazy&lt;T&gt; will be created that resolves T from the scope it was created in</li>&#xA;<li>Owned&lt;T&gt; - object resolved within a Owned&lt;T&gt; will have their disposal lifecycle tied to the Owned&lt;T&gt; (similar to autofac)</li>&#xA;<li>Meta&lt;T&gt; - objects resolved within a Meta&lt;T&gt; are resolved along with their metadata</li>&#xA;<li>Custom Delegates - any delegate that returns a type can be automatically resolved. </li>&#xA;<li>Custom interface factories with Grace.Factory</li>&#xA;</ul></li>&#xA;<li>Many LifeStyles supported including Singleton, SingletonPerScope, SingletonPerRequest (MVC4, MVC5 &amp; WCF packages), SingletonPerObjectGraph, SingletonPerAncestor&lt;T&gt;, and WeakSingleton. If none of the provided life styles meet your need you can always implement your own ICompiledLifeStyle class.</li>&#xA;<li>Built in support for the decorator pattern</li>&#xA;<li>Support for custom wrappers (Func&lt;T&gt; and Meta&lt;T&gt; are examples of built in wrappers)</li>&#xA;<li><a href="https://github.com/ipjohnson/Grace.DependencyInjection.Extensions" rel="nofollow noreferrer">ASP.Net Core</a> support</li>&#xA;<li><a href="https://github.com/ipjohnson/Grace.MVC" rel="nofollow noreferrer">ASP.Net MVC 4 &amp; 5</a> support</li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;

tcp-rst	<p><strong><em><code>RST</code></em></strong> is one of <a href="http://bxr.su/OpenBSD/sys/netinet/tcp.h#th_flags" rel="nofollow noreferrer">the eight flags</a> in the <a href="http://bxr.su/OpenBSD/sys/netinet/tcp.h#tcphdr" rel="nofollow noreferrer">TCP-header</a> that identifies that the TCP connection should be <strong><em>reset</em></strong>; colloquially, it's a small TCP packet that resets the connection, <a href="//stackoverflow.com/questions/4160347/close-vs-shutdown-socket/23483487#23483487">sent</a> when the connection gets terminated with the <a href="http://mdoc.su/-/close.2" rel="nofollow noreferrer">close(2)</a> system call.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Other common TCP header flags include <code>SYN</code>, <code>ACK</code> and <code>FIN</code>.  <a href="http://bxr.su/OpenBSD/sys/netinet/tcp_input.c#tcp_input" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Flag validity depends on the state of the TCP connection.</a></p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>References:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li><a href="http://bxr.su/OpenBSD/sys/netinet/tcp.h#TH_RST" rel="nofollow noreferrer"><code>/sys/netinet/tcp.h :: TH_RST</code></a></li>&#xA;<li><a href="http://bxr.su/OpenBSD/sys/netinet/tcp.h#th_flags" rel="nofollow noreferrer"><code>/sys/netinet/tcp.h :: th_flags</code></a></li>&#xA;<li><a href="http://bxr.su/OpenBSD/sys/netinet/tcp.h#tcphdr" rel="nofollow noreferrer"><code>/sys/netinet/tcp.h :: tcphdr</code></a></li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;

They immediately switch to the final state, showing fake data for the time while the real operation is still in-progress.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>In an optimistic update the UI behaves as though a change was successfully completed before receiving confirmation from the server that it actually was - it is being optimistic that it will eventually get the confirmation rather than an error. heroku-pipelines	<p>Each app in a pipeline represents one of the following steps in a continuous delivery workflow:  </p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li>Review </li>&#xA;<li>Development </li>&#xA;<li>Staging</li>&#xA;<li>Production</li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;&#xA;<p>A common Heroku continuous delivery workflow has the following steps:  </p>&#xA;&#xA;<ol>&#xA;<li>A developer creates a pull request to make a change to the codebase.</li>&#xA;<li>Heroku automatically creates a review app for the pull request,&#xA;allowing developers to test the change.</li>&#xA;<li>When the change is ready, its merged into the codebases master&#xA;branch.</li>&#xA;<li>The master branch is automatically deployed to staging for further&#xA;testing.</li>&#xA;<li>When its ready, the staging app is promoted to production, where&#xA;the change is available to end users of the app.</li>&#xA;</ol>&#xA;&#xA;<p>The pipelines overview page helps you visualize this flow, as well as meta information about the status of each stage. For example, you can see if your production app is running different code than staging.<br>&#xA;<a href="https://i.stack.imgur.com/4iFnd.png" rel="nofollow noreferrer"><img src="https://i.stack.imgur.com/4iFnd.png" alt="Example pipeline"></a>&#xA;<a href="https://devcenter.heroku.com/articles/pipelines" rel="nofollow noreferrer">For More Info</a></p>&#xA;

 declarations: [AppComponent, ...],&#xA;  imports: [TreeviewModule.forRoot(), ...],  &#xA;  bootstrap: [AppComponent]&#xA;})&#xA;export class AppModule {&#xA;}&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p><strong><em>Usage</em></strong></p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><em>Treeview</em>:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>&lt;ngx-treeview&#xA;    [config]="config"&#xA;    [items]="items"&#xA;    (selectedChange)="onSelectedChange($event)"&gt;&#xA;&lt;/ngx-treeview&gt;&#xA;Treeview with dropdown:&#xA;&lt;ngx-dropdown-treeview&#xA;    [config]="config"&#xA;    [items]="items"&#xA;    (selectedChange)="onSelectedChange($event)"&gt;&#xA;&lt;/ngx-dropdown-treeview&gt;&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>config is optional. This is the default configuration:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>{&#xA;   isShowAllCheckBox: true,&#xA;   isShowFilter: false,&#xA;   isShowCollapseExpand: false,&#xA;   maxHeight: 500,&#xA;   maxCount: 0,&#xA;   isShowTotal: true&#xA;}&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>You can change default configuration easily because TreeviewConfig is injectable.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><em>Pipe ngxTreeview</em>:&#xA;To map your JSON objects to TreeItem objects.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>&lt;ngx-dropdown-treeview&#xA;    [config]="config"&#xA;    [items]="items | ngxTreeview:'textField'"&#xA;    (selectedChange)="onSelectedChange($event)"&gt;&#xA;&lt;/ngx-dropdown-treeview&gt;  &#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Create a TreeviewItem:  </p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>const itCategory = new TreeviewItem({&#xA;   text: 'IT', value: 9, children: [&#xA;       {&#xA;           text: 'Programming', value: 91, children: [{&#xA;               text: 'Frontend', value: 911, children: [&#xA;                   { text: 'Angular 1', value: 9111 },&#xA;                   { text: 'Angular 2', value: 9112 },&#xA;                   { text: 'ReactJS', value: 9113 }&#xA;               ]&#xA;           }, {&#xA;               text: 'Backend', value: 912, children: [&#xA;                   { text: 'C#', value: 9121 },&#xA;                   { text: 'Java', value: 9122 },&#xA;                   { text: 'Python', value: 9123, checked: false }&#xA;               ]&#xA;           }]&#xA;       },&#xA;       {&#xA;           text: 'Networking', value: 92, children: [&#xA;               { text: 'Internet', value: 921 },&#xA;               { text: 'Security', value: 922 }&#xA;           ]&#xA;       }&#xA;   ]&#xA;});&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p><em>TreeviewEventParser</em>:  </p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Extract data from list of checked TreeviewItem and send it in parameter of event selectedChange. Some built-in TreeviewEventParser:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li>DefaultTreeviewEventParser: return values of checked items.</li>&#xA;<li>DownlineTreeviewEventParser: return list of checked items in orginal&#xA;order with their ancestors.</li>&#xA;<li>OrderDownlineTreeviewEventParser: return list of checked items in&#xA;checked order with their ancestors.
